# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I found **25 C++ source files** that implement the hot restart mechanism across the Envoy codebase:

### Key Components:

1. **Interface Definition** (`envoy/server/hot_restart.h`) - Defines the abstract HotRestart interface and exceptions

2. **Core Implementation** (source/server/):
   - `HotRestartImpl` - Main coordinator for parent/child process communication
   - `HotRestartingBase` & `RpcStream` - Unix domain socket RPC infrastructure
   - `HotRestartingParent` - Parent process that serves socket FDs and stats to child
   - `HotRestartingChild` - Child process that requests resources from parent
   - `hot_restart.proto` - Protocol definition for inter-process messages

3. **OS-Specific** (source/common/api/posix/) - Wraps POSIX syscalls for shared memory management

4. **Integration Points** (source/exe/) - Main entry points that initialize hot restart during server startup

5. **Comprehensive Tests** - Unit and integration tests validating all hot restart scenarios

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, key symbols, and a detailed explanation of how these components work together to enable zero-downtime restarts.

(envoy/server/hot_restart.h)** defines the HotRestart abstract base class that provides the public API for hot restart functionality, including methods like drainParentListeners(), duplicateParentListenSocket(), registerUdpForwardingListener(), and parentDrainedCallbackRegistrar(). It creates shared memory via attachSharedMemory(), initializes HotRestartingChild and HotRestartingParent instances, and delegates operations to them. The class maintains the base_id and restart_epoch needed for socket naming.\\n\\n2. **HotRestartingBase** (hot_restarting_base.h/cc) - The base class for both parent and child processes that handles RPC communication via Unix domain sockets. It contains the RpcStream class which manages sending and receiving HotRestartMessage protobufs over datagram sockets. Key methods include: sendHotRestartMessage() for transmitting messages with file descriptor passing support, receiveHotRestartMessage() for receiving messages, bindDomainSocket() for establishing Unix domain socket communication endpoints, and getPassedFdIfPresent() for extracting file descriptors from control data.\\n\\n3. **HotRestartingParent** (hot_restarting_parent.h/cc) - Implements parent process logic. The HotRestartingParent::Internal class handles requests from child processes including getListenSocketsForChild() which duplicates listen socket FDs to the child and exportStatsToChild() which sends parent statistics (counters, gauges, and dynamic stat name mappings) to the child.\\n\\n4. **HotRestartingChild** (hot_restarting_child.h/cc) - Implements child process logic. Key methods include: duplicateParentListenSocket() which requests socket FDs from parent, drainParentListeners() which initiates the parent drain sequence, getParentStats() which retrieves parent statistics, and mergeParentStats() which incorporates parent stats into the child's store. The child also implements Network::ParentDrainedCallbackRegistrar for registering callbacks when parent draining completes.\\n\\n5. **HotRestartNopImpl** (hot_restart_nop_impl.h) - A no-op implementation used when hot restart is disabled.\\n\\n**Protocol Definition (source/server/hot_restart.proto)** defines the HotRestartMessage protobuf format for parent-child communication. Child->parent requests include PassListenSocket (requesting socket FD), ShutdownAdmin, Stats, DrainListeners, Terminate, ForwardedUdpPacket (for QUIC UDP forwarding), and TestConnection. Parent->child replies provide matching response messages with FD data or stats information.\\n\\n**OS-Specific Implementation (source/common/api/posix/)** provides HotRestartOsSysCallsImpl (os_sys_calls_impl_hot_restart.h/cc) which wraps POSIX system calls for shared memory operations (shmOpen, shmUnlink, mmap) needed for the IPC mechanisms.\\n\\n**Entry Points** - main_common.cc uses hotRestartVersion() to report restart capability, and stripped_main_base.cc initializes HotRestartImpl during server startup, catching HotRestartDomainSocketInUseException and retrying with different base IDs on failure.\\n\\n**Test Files** validate the implementation with comprehensive test coverage including hot_restart_impl_test.cc for integration testing, hot_restarting_parent_test.cc and hot_restarting_child_test.cc for parent/child protocol validation, hot_restarting_base_test.cc for RPC stream functionality, and integration test hotrestart_test.sh for end-to-end scenarios. It creates shared memory via attachSharedMemory(), initializes HotRestartingChild and HotRestartingParent instances, and delegates operations to them. The class maintains the base_id and restart_epoch needed for socket naming.\\n\\n2. **HotRestartingBase** (hot_restarting_base.h/cc) - The base class for both parent and child processes that handles RPC communication via Unix domain sockets. It contains the RpcStream class which manages sending and receiving HotRestartMessage protobufs over datagram sockets. Key methods include: sendHotRestartMessage() for transmitting messages with file descriptor passing support, receiveHotRestartMessage() for receiving messages, bindDomainSocket() for establishing Unix domain socket communication endpoints, and getPassedFdIfPresent() for extracting file descriptors from control data.\\n\\n3. **HotRestartingParent** (hot_restarting_parent.h/cc) - Implements parent process logic. The HotRestartingParent::Internal class handles requests from child processes including getListenSocketsForChild() which duplicates listen socket FDs to the child and exportStatsToChild() which sends parent statistics (counters, gauges, and dynamic stat name mappings) to the child.\\n\\n4. **HotRestartingChild** (hot_restarting_child.h/cc) - Implements child process logic. Key methods include: duplicateParentListenSocket() which requests socket FDs from parent, drainParentListeners() which initiates the parent drain sequence, getParentStats() which retrieves parent statistics, and mergeParentStats() which incorporates parent stats into the child's store. The child also implements Network::ParentDrainedCallbackRegistrar for registering callbacks when parent draining completes.\\n\\n5. **HotRestartNopImpl** (hot_restart_nop_impl.h) - A no-op implementation used when hot restart is disabled.\\n\\n**Protocol Definition (source/server/hot_restart.proto)** defines the HotRestartMessage protobuf format for parent-child communication. Child->parent requests include PassListenSocket (requesting socket FD), ShutdownAdmin, Stats, DrainListeners, Terminate, ForwardedUdpPacket (for QUIC UDP forwarding), and TestConnection. Parent->child replies provide matching response messages with FD data or stats information.\\n\\n**OS-Specific Implementation (source/common/api/posix/)** provides HotRestartOsSysCallsImpl (os_sys_calls_impl_hot_restart.h/cc) which wraps POSIX system calls for shared memory operations (shmOpen, shmUnlink, mmap) needed for the IPC mechanisms.\\n\\n**Entry Points** - main_common.cc uses hotRestartVersion() to report restart capability, and stripped_main_base.cc initializes HotRestartImpl during server startup, catching HotRestartDomainSocketInUseException and retrying with different base IDs on failure.\\n\\n**Test Files** validate the implementation with comprehensive test coverage including hot_restart_impl_test.cc for integration testing, hot_restarting_parent_test.cc and hot_restarting_child_test.cc for parent/child protocol validation, hot_restarting_base_test.cc for RPC stream functionality, and integration test hotrestart_test.sh for end-to-end scenarios.
